"profile name": "Joshua", "profile description": "Joshua was Israel's new leader following Moses' death. It was now time to conquer the land God promised His people. The commander of the Lord's army appeared to Joshua so he knew God was with him. Joshua bravely followed God's instructions to cross the Jordan River and march around Jericho. The walls collapsed and God gave them the city!", "profile bible infoscan": "Joshua's name was Hoshea, the son of Nun, of the tribe of Ephraim, but Moses called him Joshua (\"Numbers:13:8\"). He was born as a slave in Egypt about 40 years before Moses led the Israelites out of Egypt. Joshua was Moses' military commander when the Israelites defeated the Amalekites (\"Exodus:17:8\"). He was one of the twelve spies of Israel, who along with Caleb, brought back a good report to Moses about the land of Canaan. They encouraged the Israelites to go take the land God had promised them (Numbers 13-14). Joshua and Caleb were the only two spies that God allowed to enter and possess the Promised Land after wandering in the wilderness for 40 years. Joshua was also a close aide to Moses and accompanied him part of the way up Mount Sinai when Moses received The Ten Commandments from God (\"Exodus:32:15-20\"). Before Moses' death, he made Joshua the leader of the Israelites as God had commanded. The Bible says that Joshua was filled with the Spirit of wisdom because Moses laid his hands on him (\"Deuteronomy:34:9\"). God told Joshua that He would be with him just as He was with Moses. He promised to give Joshua victory over the enemy and that no one could stand against him. The Israelites promised to follow and obey Joshua as they had obeyed Moses (Joshua 1). At the Jordan River, God told Joshua He would begin to make him a great leader in the eyes of the Israelites. By God's command, Joshua ordered the priests to carry the Ark of the Covenant to the edge of the Jordan River. The waters divided and the Israelites walked across on dry land just as they had for Moses at the Red Sea (Joshua 3). God told Joshua to take twelve stones from the dry land in the middle of the Jordan River and build an altar to God where the Israelites made camp. This altar was built to remember the miracle God performed that day. Joshua also built an altar with twelve stones in the middle of the Jordan River before the water returned (Joshua 4). \"That day the LORD made Joshua a great leader in the eyes of all the Israelites, and for the rest of his life they revered him as much as they had revered Moses.\" (\"Joshua:4:14\"). On the other side of the Jordan, near the walled city of Jericho, Joshua saw a man standing in front of him with a sword in His hand. This was the commander of the Lord's army! Joshua fell with his face to the ground in reverence and asked how he could serve Him. \"The commander of the LORD's army replied, \"Take off your sandals, for the place where you are standing is holy.\" And Joshua did as he was told.\" (\"Joshua:5:13\") Following God's specific instructions, Joshua led the Israelites to march around Jericho. \"On the seventh day the Israelites got up at dawn and marched around the town as they had done before. But this time they went around the town seven times. The seventh time around, as the priests sounded the long blast on their horns, Joshua commanded the people, 'Shout! For the Lord has given you the town!'\" (\"Joshua:6:15\"). \"When the people heard the sound of the rams' horns, they shouted as loud as they could. Suddenly, the walls of Jericho collapsed. The Israelites charged straight into the town and captured it\" (\"Joshua:6:20\"). Joshua told the two spies to go and save Rahab and her family to fulfill their promise to her. (Joshua 6:22-25) Joshua pronounced a curse of the Lord upon anyone who tried to rebuild the town of Jericho! (Joshua 6:26). God confirmed the words of Joshua by taking the lives of two men who began the rebuilding of Jericho. (\"1 Kings:16:34\"). After Jericho was defeated, Joshua led the people of Israel to conquer the Promised Land. When the Israelites fought a battle at Gibeon, Joshua asked God to cause the sun and moon to stand still so that he could finish the battle in daylight (\"Joshua:10:12\"). God also fought for the Israelites in this battle (\"Joshua:10:11\"). Joshua watched over the division of land to the different tribes of Israel. (\"Joshua:18:10\"). He died at the age of 110. This was 25 years after he entered into the Promised Land. He was buried in Timnath-serah (\"Joshua:24:28\"). Many Bible scholars view Joshua's life as a signpost that points to Jesus. The Hebrew name for Joshua is Yehoshua. Jesus' Hebrew name is Yeshua. Joshua's crossing of the Jordan is followed by Jesus' baptism in the Jordan River. Joshua's military campaigns point to Jesus' battles with Satan. Joshua's following Moses as leader of Israel points to Jesus fulfilling the Law of Moses.", "profile life lessons": "If we know that God is with us, then we know that He is for us, like he was with Joshua.", "profile key scripture": "So the Lord was with Joshua, and his reputation spread throughout the land."

"profile name": "Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego", "profile description": "Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego were three Hebrew men who trusted God and refused to bow down to worship a gold statue. They stood up boldly before King Nebuchadnezzar even when they faced sure death from the blazing furnace. God supernaturally protected the men and they were unharmed by the fire- they didn't even smell of smoke! The king was impressed and amazed by what had happened, and promoted the three men to even higher positions in Babylon!", "profile bible infoscan": "Who were these three young Hebrew men that stood up to King Nebuchadnezzar? They refused to obey his order to bow and worship his gold statue even when they faced certain death in the blazing furnace! This took place about 600 years before Jesus was born. During the third year of King Jehoiakim's reign in Judah, King Nebuchadnezzar of Babylon came to Jerusalem and attacked it. The Lord gave him victory over the King of Judah and permitted him to take tens of thousands of Israelites into captivity. Shadrach, Meshach, Abednego, were among those captured. The king ordered Ashpenaz, his chief of staff, to \"Select only strong, healthy, and good-looking young men, make sure they are well versed in every branch of learning, are gifted with knowledge and good judgment, and are suited to serve in the royal palace. Train these young men in the language and literature of Babylon.\" The king assigned them a daily ration of food and wine from his own kitchens. They were to be trained for three years, and then they would enter the royal service. (\"Daniel:1:4-5\"). The four young Jews of royal or noble birth from the tribe of Judah were among those selected to serve the king. We also find out in Daniel 1:7 that their names were changed. \"The chief of staff renamed them with these Babylonian names: Daniel was called Belteshazzar, Hananiah was called Shadrach, Mishael was called Meshach, and Azariah was called Abednego.\" Their Hebrew names were Hananiah, Mishael, and Azariah. Hananiah means \"God who is gracious.\" Mishael means \"Who is like God?\" It also means \"to feed\" or \"to provide\" - as in how a husband provides for his family. Azariah appropriately means \"God has helped.\" The Hebrew men were determined not to eat the king's royal food and wine to not defile themselves according to Jewish law. They asked the king's chief of staff to allow them to instead eat vegetables and water for ten days. After that time, he could compare them to the other men who ate the king's diet. The chief of staff reluctantly agreed to the test. (\"Daniel:1:8-14\"). \"At the end of the ten days, Daniel and his three friends looked healthier and better nourished than the young men who had been eating the food assigned by the king. So after that, the attendant fed them only vegetables instead of the food and wine provided for the others.\" (\"Daniel:1:16\"). After the training period, all of the men were brought before the king. Daniel 1:19-20 says, \"The king talked with them, and no one impressed him as much as Daniel, Hananiah, Mishael, and Azariah. So they entered the royal service. Whenever the king consulted them in any matter requiring wisdom and balanced judgment, he found them ten times more capable than any of the magicians and enchanters in his entire kingdom.\" When Daniel successfully interpreted King Nebuchadnezzar's dream, the king was thrilled and rewarded him. Daniel did not forget his three friends! \"Then the king appointed Daniel to a high position and gave him many valuable gifts. He made Daniel ruler over the whole province of Babylon, as well as chief over all his wise men. At Daniel's request, the king appointed Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego to be in charge of all the affairs of the province of Babylon, while Daniel remained in the king's court.\" (\"Daniel:2:48-49\"). All seemed to be going smoothly until the king built a huge gold statue. He required everyone to bow down and worship it whenever the music played. Anyone who disobeyed would be thrown into a blazing furnace! Some of the king's wise men, who were no doubt jealous of Daniel and his friends, noticed Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego refused to bow and worship. They had the nerve to defy the king's order at the dedication of the prized new statue! They gladly informed the king of their rebellion. He was furious and demanded that the three men come before him. Shadrach, Meshach, Abednego did not back down and said: \"O Nebuchadnezzar, we do not need to defend ourselves before you in this matter. If we are thrown into the blazing furnace, the God we serve is able to save us from it, and He will rescue us from your hand, O king. But even if He does not, we want you to know, O king, that we will not serve your gods or worship the image of gold you have set up\" (\"Daniel:3:16-18\"). Nebuchadnezzar's face was distorted in rage! He ordered that the furnace be heated seven times hotter than usual. Soldiers were ordered to firmly bind the fully clothed Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego and cast them in the blazing furnace. Because the king in his anger had demanded such a hot fire, the flames killed the soldiers as they threw the three men into the furnace. Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, securely tied, fell into the roaring flames. (\"Daniel:3:1-25\"). Was the story over? Not with God in control! As the king watched the execution, he suddenly jumped up, amazed. There were now four people in the fire walking around unharmed! The fourth person looked like a god! The king then said, \"Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, servants of the Most High God, come out! Come here!\" (\"Daniel:3:26\"). The young men then emerged from the fiery furnace not even smelling of smoke. King Nebuchadnezzar the exclaimed, \"Praise to the God of Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego! He sent his angel to rescue his servants who trusted in him. They defied the king's command and were willing to die rather than serve or worship any god except their own God\" (\"Daniel:3:28\"). Then the king promoted Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego to even higher positions in the province of Babylon. (\"Daniel:3:30\").", "profile life lessons": "Take a stand for God.", "profile key scripture": "\"But even if he doesn't, we want to make it clear to you, Your Majesty, that we will never serve your gods or worship the gold statue you have set up.\""
"profile name": "The Spirit of God", "profile description": "The Spirit of God is the Holy Spirit. He filled the believers who were in the upstairs room in Jerusalem on the Day of Pentecost. He fills us with power to witness and to live according to God's Word.", "profile bible infoscan": "The Spirit of God is the Holy Spirit. He is the third person of the Trinity (Three-in-One God). There is God the Father, God the Son, and God the Holy Spirit. The Hebrew word for the Spirit of God is \"Ruach Elohim,\" which means \"breath\" or \"breathing out.\" Breath is a good word to describe God because breath represents life, a living creative force. When God created the heaven and the earth, the \"Spirit of God was hovering over the surface of the waters\" (\"Genesis:1:2\"), and \"then the Lord God formed the man from the dust of the ground. He breathed the breath of life into the man's nostrils and the man became a living person\" (\"Genesis:2:7\"). The Spirit of God was present throughout history. God told Moses he had \"filled Bezalel with the Spirit of God, giving him great wisdom, ability, and expertise in all kinds of craft\" (\"Exodus:31:3\"), which he would use in the building of the Tabernacle and the Ark. The Spirit of God also came upon Balaam (\"Genesis:1:2\" , \"Numbers:24:2\"), Saul (\"1 Samuel:11:6\"), messengers (\"1 Samuel:19:20\"), Azariah (\"2 Chronicles:15:1\"), and Zechariah (\"2 Chronicles:24:20\"). When Jesus was baptized by John, the Spirit of God came down like a dove and settled on Him while God's voice spoke, \"This is my dearly loved Son, who brings me great joy\" (\"Matthew:3:16-17\"). When Jesus ascended into heaven after His death and resurrection, Jesus promised the gift of the Holy Spirit and His power (\"Acts:1:8\"). The work of the Spirit of God is to convict us of sin (\"John:16:8\"), to live in believers (\"John:14:15-17\"), to guide believers in all truth (\"John:16:13\"), to give spiritual gifts to believers (\"1 Corinthians:12\"), to reveal the deep things of God, and to strengthen, comfort, encourage, guide, and empower the children of God. In his letter to the Romans, Paul encourages the Christians to live in the Spirit: \"For all who are led by the Spirit of God are children of God\" (\"Romans:8:14\"). The apostle John warns Christians to be aware of false prophets who do not have the Spirit of God (\"1 John:4:2-4\"). In the Book of Revelation, the phrase \"seven Spirits of God\" or the \"sevenfold Spirit of God\" is mentioned four times (\"Revelation:1:4\" , \"Revelation:3:1\" , \"Revelation:4:5\" , \"Revelation:5:6\"). Seven is considered God's number of perfection, and there are different interpretations of the phrase \"Spirits of God.\" In \"Isaiah:11:2\" , the work of the Spirit is described as seven-fold: the spirit of the Lord, wisdom, understanding, counsel, might, knowledge, the fear of the Lord. These \"seven Spirits\" are interpreted by some scholars as being the Seven Spirits of God described in the Book of Revelation. The Holy Spirit works in our lives to perfect us. In \"2 Peter:1:5-11\" , the sevenfold character of God is described through Christ: moral excellence, knowledge, self-control, patient endurance, godliness, brotherly affection, and love for everyone. Some scholars believe that these refer to the seven Spirits of God.", "profile life lessons": "Allow the Spirit of God to bring you to Christ, to live in you, and to work in your life.", "profile key scripture": "\"But you will receive power when the Holy Spirit comes upon you. And you will be my witnesses, telling people about me everywhere - In Jerusalem, throughout Judea, in Samaria and to the ends of the earth.\""

Regardless of his nickname, there was no doubt that Thomas loved Jesus! Are you going there again?\" After seeing that Jesus was determined to go, Thomas boldly showed his love and loyalty. Thomas, nicknamed the Twin, said to his fellow disciples, \"Let's go, too - and die with Jesus.\" (\"John:11:9\"). At the Last Supper, Jesus shared with His disciples that He was going to heaven to prepare a home for them. Jesus said that they knew the way to heaven. Thomas and the other disciples didn't understand what Jesus was saying. \"No, we don't know, Lord,\" Thomas said. \"We have no idea where you are going, so how can we know the way?\" (\"John:14:1-5\"). Soon after Jesus rose from the dead, He appeared to ten of the disciples. Thomas was not present. The disciples then shared with Thomas that they had seen the Lord. Thomas refused to believe until he could see and feel the wounds received by Jesus on the cross. (\"John:20:19-25\"). Eight days later the disciples were together again, and this time Thomas was with them. The doors were locked; but suddenly, as before, Jesus was standing among them. \"Peace be with you,\" he said. Then he said to Thomas, \"Put your finger here, and look at my hands. Put your hand into the wound in my side. Don't be faithless any longer. Believe!\" \"My Lord and my God!\" Thomas exclaimed. Then Jesus told him, \"You believe because you have seen me. Blessed are those who believe without seeing me.\" (John 20:26-29). Thomas was not a doubter any longer! "profile name": "Altar", "profile description": "", "profile bible infoscan": "The Hebrew word for altar means \"a place of slaughter or sacrifice.\" An altar is a table, platform, or elevated place on which a priest placed a sacrifice as an offering to God. The word 'altar' is used 433 times in the Bible, so it must be pretty important. The first altar was built by Noah after the Flood (\"Genesis:8:20\"). Several altars are mention in Genesis in connection with Abraham. His first altar at Shechem seemed to be a symbol of his possession of the land (\"Genesis:12:7\"). At his altars between Bethel and Ai (\"Genesis:12:8\"), and at Hebron (\"Genesis:13:18\"), Abraham sacrificed animals and called upon the name of the Lord. His last altar was built on top of a mountain in Moriah (\"Genesis:22:9\") where he intended to sacrifice Isaac. Not all the altars in the Old Testament were used to offer sacrifices. They were also used to remind the Israelites of important events in their history (\"Joshua:22:26-29\"). During the days of Moses, there were two altars that the priests used: the altar of burnt offering (\"Exodus:27:1-8\" and \"Exodus:40:6\") and the altar of incense (\"Exodus:30:1-10\"). No altars are recognized in the New Testament Church. The 'altar' in \"Hebrews:13:10\" refers to Jesus as being the altar of each believer.", "profile life lessons": "", "profile key scripture": "\"When they arrived at the place where God had told him to go, Abraham built an altar and arranged the wood on it. Then he tied his son, Isaac, and laid him on the altar on top of the wood.\""
"profile name": "The Cross", "profile description": "", "profile bible infoscan": "The cross was an upright wooden stake or post with a crossbeam. It was used as an instrument of humiliation, torture, and execution for criminals. It was the form of execution used by the Romans in New Testament times. Those sentenced to death on a cross were usually beaten with leather lashes. Victims were then forced to carry the upper crossbeam to the execution site where the central stake was already set up. After being tied with ropes or nailed to the crossbeam through the wrists, the victim was then hoisted with the crossbeam against that stake. A block or peg was sometimes fastened to the stake as a seat, and the feet were then tied or nailed to the stake. Death by suffocation or exhaustion normally followed only after a period of agonizing pain. Jesus was crucified on a cross. The cross is a symbol of His willingness to suffer for our sins so that our relationship with God can be restored. We are reconciled to God (\"2 Corinthians:5:19\" , \"Colossians:1:20\"). It is thus a symbol of Jesus' love and God's power to save.", "profile life lessons": "", "profile key scripture": "And through him God reconciled everything to himself. He made peace with everything in heaven and on earth by means of Christ's blood on the cross."

"profile name": "Hophni and Phinehas", "profile description": "The Book of 1 Samuel describes Hophni as an officiating priest at the sanctuary of Shiloh, along with his brother, Phinehas. In the Biblical narrative, Hophni and Phinehas are criticized for engaging in illicit behavior, such as taking the best portion of sacrifices for themselves. Their misdeeds led to a divine curse being put on them. They both died on the same day, during a battle against the Philistines at Ebenezer.", "profile bible infoscan": "Two brothers, Hophni and Phinehas, were Israelite priests at the Tabernacle in Shiloh. They were sons of the priest Eli. The Bible calls them scoundrels who had no respect for the Lord or for their positions as priests (\"1 Samuel:2:12\"). The two men were wicked and committed terrible sins as they officiated the worship and the offering of sacrifices by the Israelites at the Tabernacle. The sons took by force the portion of meat that was reserved for God and ate it themselves. They also took the fat portion of the meat that was supposed to be burnt before the Lord. This was forbidden according to God's law. The sin of Eli's sons was very serious in the Lord's sight! (Leviticus 7:30-34; 1 Samuel 2:12 - 17). The Bible says that Eli was very old, but he knew about the sins of his sons and did not restrain them. Eli heard the bad reports from the people who told him the wicked deeds his sons were doing at the Tabernacle. Eli confronted them with their sin and told them to stop; however, it was not enough in God's eyes. In 1 Samuel 3:13 the Lord spoke to Samuel about Eli: \"I have warned him that judgment is coming upon his family forever, because his sons are blaspheming God and he hasn't disciplined them.\" Hophni and Phinehas would not listen to their father. The Bible tells us that God was already planning for them to die because of their disobedience, disrespect, and sin. God then sent a prophet to Eli to declare judgment on his family for the sin of his sons. (\"1 Samuel:2:22\"). God also revealed that Eli wasn't completely innocent! Eli also enjoyed the meat from the offerings that belonged to the Lord! 1 Samuel 2: 29 says, \"So why do you scorn my sacrifices and offerings? Why do you give your sons more honor than you give me - for you and they have become fat from the best offerings of my people Israel!\" The prophet told Eli that Hophni and Phinehas would both die on the same day to prove that His words were true. (\"1 Samuel:2:24\"). God then later spoke to Eli through Samuel and confirmed to Eli that He was about to do as He had warned; judgment was coming to Eli's family! 1 Samuel 3:14 says, \"So I have vowed that the sins of Eli and his sons will never be forgiven by sacrifices or offerings.\" That tells us just how wicked Hophni and Phinehas' were and how much they angered God! "profile name": "The Sacrifice", "profile description": "", "profile bible infoscan": "A sacrifice is an act of killing an animal or surrendering a possession as an offering to a god. Although the main purpose of the sacrifice is to please the deity (god) and gain his or her favor, it can often express faith, repentance, and worship. The pagans in ancient times offered their sacrifices to gods and idols -- but the Israelites made offerings to the Living God. The heads of the families and the priests brought the sacrifices into the Temple in Jerusalem where the sacrifices were offered. However, sacrifices have not been offered by the Jews since the destruction of the Temple by Romans in A.D. 70. Usually, the burnt offering was a lamb -- but sometimes a ewe or ram was sacrificed. The animal could not be sick or dying. It had to be perfect. These Old Testament sacrifices (including the intended sacrifice of Isaac) all point to the sacrifice of Jesus Christ (\"Hebrews:9\" is the perfect sacrifice, the perfect gift. "profile name": "The Flood", "profile description": "", "profile bible infoscan": "God was about to punish the wickedness of the world by a flood that would cover the earth! (Genesis 6:5-8). God told Noah, the only righteous person on earth, to build an ark to hold his family and all types of animals. When the boat was finished, Noah, his family, and the animals went inside. The rain started 7 days later. (\"Genesis:7:1-4\"). Noah's flood was much more than any 40-day rainstorm could ever be. \"When Noah was 600 years old, on the seventeenth day of the second month, all the underground waters erupted from the earth, and the rain fell in mighty torrents from the sky. The rain continued to fall for forty days and forty nights and the floodwaters covered the earth for 150 days. (\"Genesis:7:11-12\"). \"As the waters rose higher and higher above the ground, the boat floated safely on the surface. Finally, the water covered even the highest mountains on the earth, rising more than twenty-two feet above the highest peaks. All the living things on earth died - birds, domestic animals, wild animals, small animals that scurry along the ground, and all the people.\" (\"Genesis:7:18-21\"). The parable of the Prodigal Son illustrates God's love, mercy, and forgiveness to all who have sinned and are lost.", "profile bible infoscan": "A parable is a short story which uses familiar events to illustrate a religious or ethical point. Parable comes from a Greek word that means to place one thing beside the other to compare them. Parables can be found throughout the Bible. In the Old Testament, one well known example is when God sent Nathan the prophet to King David. Nathan told a story about a rich man and a poor man and compared it to the sin of David with Bathsheba. David's eyes were opened causing him to repent before God. (\"2 Samuel:12:1-4\"). In the New Testament, Jesus commonly taught in parables. His story about the Prodigal Son is one parable. The Prodigal or Lost Son is one of three stories Jesus told about being lost and found. The other parables were the Lost Sheep and the Lost Coin. Jesus told these stories to the religious leaders when they complained about Him hanging out with sinful people - and even eating with them! In the Prodigal Son parable, the younger son represents sinners who turn away from God and make unwise choices. The father represents God, our heavenly Father. Parables were Jesus' main method of teaching while on the earth. (\"John:15:1-32\"). \"Mark:4:34\" says, \"Jesus used many similar stories and illustrations to teach the people as much as they could understand. In fact, in His public ministry He never taught without using parables; but afterward, when He was alone with His disciples, He explained everything to them.\" Jesus' parables refer to simple things, yet they deal with major religious themes, such as the growth of the Kingdom of God, the importance of prayer, and the meaning of love. Jesus' disciples asked Him about the parables He taught. \"He replied, \"You are permitted to understand the secret of the Kingdom of God. But I use parables for everything I say to outsiders, so that the Scriptures might be fulfilled: 'When they see what I do, they will learn nothing. When they hear what I say, they will not understand. Otherwise, they will turn to Me and be forgiven.\" (\"Mark:4:11-12\"). Parables cause us to dig deeper to understand and apply what is being taught to our own lives.", "profile life lessons": "We need to pay attention to the truth that God will show us through the common things in our lives.", "profile key scripture": "In fact, in his public ministry he never taught without using parables."

"profile name": "Burlap and Ashes", "profile description": "The king of Nineveh heard Jonah's message of doom. He took off his royal robes and put on sackcloth (burlap) to humble himself. He declared a fast and all of the people, including the animals, wore sackcloth and mourned. God saw what they did and changed His mind and spared the city from judgment!", "profile bible infoscan": "Burlap was most often made of coarse camel or goat hair. The material was used to make grain bags known as sackcloth. It also was customarily worn to mourn a death, or as a sign of deep repentance, anguish, and humility. Since burlap is a coarse material, it would be very uncomfortable to wear. Wearing sackcloth was often preceded by tearing one's clothes. It was also frequently worn together with ashes which were sat in, smeared, or sprinkled on the body or head. (\"2 Samuel:3:31\"). The Bible has many examples of people who wore sackcloth (burlap) along with ashes for a number of different circumstances. In the story of Jonah, the Ninevites, including the king, wore sackcloth and ashes as a sign of repentance for sin. (\"Jonah:3:5-6\"). In the Ninevites case, even the animals wore sackcloth. (\"Jonah:3:8\"). Examples of sackcloth and ashes being worn in the Bible: - To signify repentance of sin: \"1 Kings:21:27\" ; \"1 Chronicles:21:16\" ; \"Jeremiah:6:26\" ; \"Lamentations:2:10\" . - As a sign of mourning for the dead: \"Genesis:37:34\" ; \"2 Samuel:3:31\" . - At times of prayer for deliverance: \"2 Kings:19:1-2\" , \"Daniel:9:3\" . - As a sign of mourning for personal or national disaster, or devastating news: \"Job:16:15\" ; \"Esther:4:1\" ; \"Isaiah:37:1\" ; \"1 Kings:21:27\" . John, in \"Revelation:11:3\" , tells us that the two witnesses will be clothed in burlap as they prophesy in the end times. Sackcloth and ashes were an indication of a person's emotions and an outward sign of a person's inward condition. They represented a change of heart as they humbled themselves before God. David spoke of how God honored his time in of true mourning and repentance in Psalm 30:11. \"You have turned my mourning into joyful dancing. "profile name": "Rahab", "profile description": "Israelite spies hid in Rahab's house. When the king's men came looking for the spies, Rahab protected them. Her sacrifice and reverence for God gave her favor when the Isrealites eventually conquered the land.", "profile bible infoscan": "In the story of Joshua and the battle of Jericho, Rahab was a woman who hid the two Israelite spies. She hid the spies under bundles of flax on her roof. She then lied to the king's men, telling them that the men had been there but had left Jericho before the gates were closed. Before the spies went to sleep that night, Rahab went up on the roof to talk with them. She said: \"I know the LORD has given you this land. We are all afraid of you. Everyone in the land is living in terror. For we have heard how the LORD made a dry path for you through the Red Sea when you left Egypt. And we know what you did to Sihon and Og, the two Amorite kings east of the Jordan River, whose people you completely destroyed. No wonder our hearts have melted in fear! No one has the courage to fight after hearing such things. For the LORD your God is the supreme God of the heavens above and the earth below\" (\"Joshua:2:8-11\"). That is quite a confession of faith! Rahab believed in the God of the Hebrews and begged for her life and for her family. The spies offered their lives as a guarantee for her safety, as well as her family if she did not betray them. The spies instructed her to leave a scarlet cord hanging in her window so it could be identified during the attack. This protection would also be for her entire family if they remained in her house. Rahab agreed to their terms. Rahab's house was built into the town wall, so she let the spies down by a rope through the window. They escaped to the hill country where they hid for three days from the men searching for them. After helping the spies escape, Rahab left the scarlet rope hanging from the window. (\"Joshua:2:14\"). Rahab tied the scarlet cord in the window so everyone could see it. She believed the spies' promise and acted upon it immediately, not knowing when the attack would come. She put her faith in God - and also in the promise of God's people. When the walls of Jericho collapsed, Joshua sent the two spies to rescue Rahab her whole family as they had promised. \"The men who had been spies went in and brought out Rahab, her father, mother, brothers, and all the other relatives who were with her. They moved her whole family to a safe place near the camp of Israel. Then the Israelites burned the town and everything in it. Only the things made from silver, gold, bronze, or iron were kept for the treasury of the Lord's house. So Joshua spared Rahab the prostitute and her relatives who were with her in the house, because she had hidden the spies Joshua sent to Jericho. And she lives among the Israelites to this day.\" (\"Joshua:6:22\"). Hundreds of years later, her name shows up on the first page of the New Testament when Matthew gives the genealogy of Jesus: \"Salmon the father of Boaz, whose mother was Rahab, Boaz the father of Obed, whose mother was Ruth, Obed the father of Jesse, and Jesse the father of King David\" (\"Matthew:1:5-6\"). This means Rahab is part of Jesus' family tree! Rahab is also listed as one of the Heroes of Faith. \"It was by faith that Rahab the prostitute was not destroyed with the people in her city who refused to obey God. For she had given a friendly welcome to the spies\" (\"Hebrews:11:31\"). The fact that Rahab had a sinful past and was accepted by her faith should encourage us all. Everyone in the city lost their lives except for Rahab and her family. This shows that by faith in Christ, our old life is gone, and our new life begins. "profile name": "The Temple", "profile description": "There have been two temples in the history of the Jewish people, Solomon's Temple, and The Second Temple, which was built by King Herod. These temples stood on Mount Moriah, or the Temple Mount in Jerusalem.", "profile bible infoscan": "The Temple is a place of worship. It is regarded as a dwelling place for the presence of God. There have been three Temples in Jerusalem. The first was built by Solomon and called Solomon's Temple. It is known as the First Temple. King David desired to build a Temple for God. He made plans to build it and even gathered materials to construct it. But, God would not allow him to actually build it. Instead, God allowed David's son Solomon to build it. (\"1 Chronicles;22:1-19\" 19). The temple was dedicated to Yahweh and it housed the Ark of the Covenant. This was a huge celebration and dedication ceremony where God's presence filled the Temple. The priests could not even continue to minister! (1 Kings 8). Solomon's Temple was destroyed by the Babylonians many years after its construction in 587 BC. (2 Kings 25:1-21). The Second Temple, called Zerubbabel's Temple, was rebuilt on the same site by orders of King Cyrus of Persia. The building was stopped once because of opposition and then restarted again. (Ezra 1:1-5; Ezra 5:12). The Third Temple is also called the Jerusalem Temple. It was rebuilt by Herod the Great. He remodeled the Temple and surrounding courts starting in about 20 BC. The temple location was on or near the Dome of Rock which now stands in Jerusalem. In the Temple was the Holy Place and the Holy of Holies. This Temple was where Zechariah served and was burning incense when Gabriel appeared to him to prophesy John the Baptizer's birth. By this time, the Ark of the Covenant had disappeared. In the temple court was the Altar of sacrifice. Inside the Holy Place was the Menorah, a seven-branched lampstand. The lower levels of the Western wall, or Wailing Wall, are what remain of Herod's Temple today. Mary and Joseph brought Jesus to the Temple to present Him to the Lord. ((\"Luke:2:21-39\"). When Jesus was twelve years old, His parents discovered Him in the Temple after the Passover celebration. \"Three days later they finally discovered him in the Temple, sitting among the religious teachers, listening to them and asking questions.\" Jesus responded to his parent's. \"Didn't you know that I must be in my Father's house?\" (Luke 2:45-46, 49). After Jesus' ministry began, He entered the Temple and drove the merchants out. He then knocked over the tables and chairs of the money changers. He said to them, \"The Scriptures declare, 'My Temple will be called a house of prayer,' but you have turned it into a den of thieves!\" (\"Matthew:21:12-13\"). Jesus said that she gave more than all the rest of them because she gave everything she had. (Luke 21:1-4). Jesus declared Himself to be even greater than the Temple in Matthew 12:6. Talking to the Samaritan woman at the well, Jesus declared that people will worship God in Spirit and Truth. It would no longer matter where you worship God, the Father. (Luke 4:21-24). Jesus predicted the Temple's destruction. (Mark 13:2). Stephen preached that God doesn't live in temples made by human hands. Through the power of the Holy Spirit, Peter performed miracles. He healed a crippled beggar (\"Acts:3:1-11\") and many others (\"Acts:5:12-16\"). He was imprisoned for preaching about Jesus, but he escaped miraculously (\"Acts:12:6-19\"). After seeing a vision, Peter was the first to take the Gospel to the Gentiles (Acts 10). He played a key role at the council of Jerusalem (Acts 15, Galatians 2). Here it was decided that Gentiles could become church members without first becoming Jews. Peter wrote two letters, 1 Peter and 2 Peter. These are often called epistles. In the letters he encouraged the readers facing persecution and suffering for their faith. He urged them to live as people who belong to Christ. "profile name": "The Law of the Medes and Persians", "profile description": "", "profile bible infoscan": "Media was the name of an ancient country in Asia. It is now included in parts of Iran, Iraq, and Turkey. The history of the Medes is complex because it involved many alliances with several nations, as well as the rise and fall of these nations. During the era of Nebuchadnezzar and the time of the prophet Jeremiah (about 605-552 B.C.), the Median kingdom was at the height of its power. It dominated Persia until the time of Cyrus, the founder of the Persian Empire. Cyrus defeated Media in 549 B.C. However, Media remained the most important province and the dual name, \"Medes and Persians,\" was used. This term \"The Laws of the Medes and Persians\" was used to describe unchangeable laws. Even the king was powerless to change a law. We read about the unalterable Laws of the Medes and Persians in \"Esther:1:19\" and \"Daniel:6:8\" .", "profile life lessons": "", "profile key scripture": "\"And now, Your Majesty, issue and sign this law so it cannot be changed, an official law of the Medes and Persians that cannot be revoked.\""

King Herod built the third temple, and this is the Temple Jesus visited after He rode into Jerusalem on a donkey. He proclaimed the Word of the Lord in a time when the worship of idols was gaining strength. Elijah is regarded as one of the most powerful Old Testament prophets. He did not shy away from speaking God's Word to kings and other leaders. He was similar in rugged appearance to John the Baptist (\"2 Kings:1:8\"). God told Elijah to hide by the Kerith Brook by God's direction after delivering the message about the drought to King Ahab. God then commanded ravens to bring meat to Elijah to eat. God told Elijah to leave the brook when the water dried up and travel to Zarephath to stay with a widow. Through Elijah, God performed a miracle to provide endless flour and oil to the widow and her son to eat until the drought ended. This was to reward her faith for opening her house to Elijah, and by faith, giving him her last meal. Elijah raised the widow's son to life after he became sick and died (I Kings 17). Elijah is sometimes referred to as the prophet of fire. He called down fire twice to destroy soldiers sent by an evil king that had come to arrest Elijah after he delivered God's Word of judgment to the king (\"2 Kings:1:1-12\"). Elijah also called down fire from heaven when he challenged King Ahab, Jezebel, and the 850 prophets of Baal and Asherah on Mount Carmel. The fire burnt up the water soaked sacrifice, the stone altar, and even the ground around the altar. Through this bold act of Elijah's faith and trust in God, the people turned to God and cried out, \"The Lord, He is God!\" Then Elijah commanded the people to seize all the prophets of Baal and have them killed in the Kishon Valley. (\"1 Kings:18:16-40\"). After the confrontation with Ahab, Elijah prayed, and the rain fell on Israel for the first time in more than three years. Then the God's Spirit came upon Elijah, giving him special strength to outrun Ahab's chariot all the way back to the entrance of Jezreel! (\"1 Kings:18:41-45\"). Elijah was a bold prophet, yet he still was human. Jezebel was furious that Elijah had killed her prophets, and she vowed to kill him. (\"Joshua:6:1-21\"). In Deuteronomy 9:1-3, God had warned the Israelites what was ahead of them as they entered the Promised Land. \"Listen, O Israel! Just how large were the walls around the city? Excavations at the site have revealed the stone wall around the city to be about 12-15 high. On top of this wall was a second, mud brick wall approximately six feet thick and around 20-26 feet tall. Imagine silently marching around the bottom of this fortress as the enemy stares down at you! The site of Jericho has undergone four major archaeological excavations. It has been shown that Jericho's mud brick walls crumpled in a heap at the base of the retaining wall. According to the Archaeological Study Bible, excavations point to an earthquake taking place. The fallen bricks formed a ramp that the Israelites used to enter the city. Archaeologists also have determined that a massive fire took place. They uncovered a layer of ash and charred debris roughly three feet thick. (\"Joshua:6:24\"). The time of the invasion of Jericho was also confirmed to be around harvest time. Full jars of recently harvested grain were found in the excavations. This showed that Israel's siege was short: seven days versus months. In a longer siege, the food supplies would be depleted. This also supports the Biblical account of the sudden, catastrophic wall collapse. Daily life was going on as usual until the moment the Israelites shouted and the wall collapsed. (Joshua 3:15; Joshua 6). Rahab's house was located within the fortifications of the city on the outer wall. The spies had promised to protect Rahab and her family inside her house. Amazingly, archaeologists found a section of the wall in the lower city that did not fall. Ruins were found during the German excavations (1907 to 1909) of a wall, possibly eight feet tall, with houses built against it. ", "profile bible infoscan": "A scribe is someone who writes and records important documents, events, records, and decisions. In the Old Testament, scribes were wise men who often counseled and advised kings. They held important positions of authority and influence in the government. They prepared and issued decrees, contracts, and letters by the king's authority. These men were also called court secretaries or historians. (\"2 Samuel:8:17\" ; \"1 Chronicles:18:16\"). A man named Baruch was a scribe that was a companion to the prophet Jeremiah. \"So Jeremiah sent for Baruch son of Neriah, and as Jeremiah dictated all the prophecies that the Lord had given him, Baruch wrote them on a scroll.\" (\"Jeremiah:36:4\"). A scribe named Ezra worked alongside Nehemiah as the walls of Jerusalem were rebuilt. (\"Ezra:7:6\"). The scribes became experts in copying, interpreting, and preserving the law. Can you imagine a world without computers, copiers, and printers? The scribes did all their work without them! This is why a scribe's work was so important. We can thank the Jewish scribes for preserving the Old Testament section of our Bibles. Many of the scribes in the New Testament were Pharisees. They were also called lawyers, and experts or teachers of the Law. Yet, the scribes began to go beyond copying and interpreting Scripture. They began to add manmade traditions to God's Law. Some of these traditions were even considered to be more important than the Law itself! Instead of preserving God's Word, their traditions actually nullified or canceled it out! Jesus said, \"And so you cancel the word of God in order to hand down your own tradition. And this is only one example among many others.\" (\"Mark:7:13\"). The scribes were hypocrites at heart. They were more interested in appearing good to men than pleasing God. Outward holiness replaced a life of true inward purity and godliness. This led to many confrontations between Jesus and the religious leaders. They thought Jesus showed disrespect for their customs and traditions. They closely watched Jesus for things that were against the religious customs. As an example, when Jesus healed a crippled man on the Sabbath, He told the man to pick up his mat and walk. Carrying a mat was considered work and so it was against their religious customs! (\"John:5:15\"). He said they didn't even obey what they told others to do! Wherever Jesus traveled, the religious leaders tried to trick and trap Him. They wanted to discredit Him. The people saw a difference between Jesus and the scribes, Pharisees and Sadducees. Jesus spoke the truth and lived it as well. Another difference that attracted people to Jesus was that Jesus taught with real authority! The scribes always quoted a previous great legal authority for their decisions and teaching. Jesus taught with his own personal authority given by God the Father. He did not need to quote any so called experts! This angered Jewish religious leaders. (\"Mark:1:22\"). Not all Scribes opposed Jesus and His followers; A Pharisee named Gamaliel was one. (\"Acts:5:34\"). Eventually the religious leaders, including the scribes, had enough of Jesus and His followers. Gideon obeyed God and tore down his father's altar to Baal and the Asherah pole used for worship. He then built an altar to The Lord there. This made the people angry and demanded that Gideon be put to death. God protected Gideon; his father intervened on his behalf to silence the angry mob. From that time they called him Jerub-baal, which means \"Let Baal defend himself,\" because Gideon broke down Baal's altar. (\"Judges:6:25-32\"). As the enemy's armies camped near the Israelites, preparing to attack, The Spirit of the Lord clothed Gideon with power. Gideon blew a ram's horn calling the warriors from the tribes of Israel to assemble for battle. Gideon still needed more proof from God that He was calling him to rescue His people. Gideon laid out a test to God. \"Then Gideon said to God, \"If you are truly going to use me to rescue Israel as you promised, prove it to me in this way. I will put a wool fleece on the threshing floor tonight. If the fleece is wet with dew in the morning but the ground is dry, then I will know that you are going to help me rescue Israel as you promised.\" And that is just what happened. When Gideon got up early the next morning, he squeezed the fleece and wrung out a whole bowlful of water. Then Gideon said to God, \"Please don't be angry with me, but let me make one more request. Let me use the fleece for one more test. This time let the fleece remain dry while the ground around it is wet with dew.\" So that night God did as Gideon asked. The fleece was dry in the morning, but the ground was covered with dew. (\"Judges:6:36-40\"). How kind and patient God was with Gideon! Gideon's army consisted of 32,000 warriors and God told Gideon that his army was too large. God said that with an army this size, they could boast that they defeated the enemy by their own strength instead of giving credit to God. God told Gideon that any man who was timid or afraid could go home. 22,000 men went home leaving only 10,000 with Gideon. Then God told Gideon to perform another test to reduce the army even more! 9700 men were eliminated this time, leaving Gideon only 300 men! (\"Judges:7:1-7\"). After this, God told Gideon to get up and go. However, if he was still afraid to attack the enemy, he could take Purah, his servant, and go to the enemy camp. Once there, God would encourage him and make him eager to attack. God caused Gideon to hear a dream and interpretation by some enemy soldiers. After hearing the soldiers speak, he was finally convinced that God was giving him the victory! Gideon bowed to worship God and then ran to prepare his 300 troops. Gideon divided the men into three groups of 100 each. He gave them each a ram's horn, a clay jar and a torch. \"It was just after midnight, after the changing of the guard, when Gideon and the 100 men with him reached the edge of the Midianite camp. Suddenly, they blew the ram's' horns and broke their clay jars. Then all three groups blew their horns and broke their jars. They held the blazing torches in their left hands and the horns in their right hands, and they all shouted, \"A sword for the Lord and for Gideon!\" Each man stood at his position around the camp and watched as all the Midianites rushed around in a panic, shouting as they ran to escape. When the 300 Israelites blew their rams' horns, the Lord caused the warriors in the camp to fight against each other with their swords. Those who were not killed fled to places as far away as Beth-shittah near Zererah and to the border of Abel-meholah near Tabbath.\" (\"Judges:7:19-22\"). Gideon and his men then chased the men who escaped until they captured or killed them. (\"Judges:7:23\"). After Gideon returned from battle, the people tried to make him their ruler. Haman turned pale; shocked and then terrified to hear Esther's secret that Mordecai had told her to keep until such a time as this! The king ordered Haman hanged on the very gallows he had built to execute Mordecai. What a turn of events! (\"Esther:7:1-10\"). On that same day, King Xerxes gave Haman's property to Queen Esther. Then Mordecai was brought before the king because Esther told the king how they were related. The king took off his signet ring and gave it to Mordecai. Esther appointed Mordecai to be in charge of Haman's property.Then Esther went again before the king and begged him to stop the evil plot of Haman against the Jews. Then King told Esther and Mordecai to send a message to the Jews in his name and seal it with his signet ring. The message they wrote gave the Jews authority to defend themselves when they were attacked. The Jews overpowered their enemies and Haman's plan was defeated! Esther wasn't done yet; she asked for the bodies of Haman's ten sons to be hung from the gallows he had constructed. Esther and Mordecai then established an annual celebration called, the Feast of Purim, to remember the defeat of Haman and their victory over their enemies. ( Esther 8-9). Purim is still celebrated today with the entire book of Esther read in synagogues around the world. He was given authority, honor, and sovereignty over all the nations of the world, so that people of every race and nation and language would obey Him. His rule is eternal - it will never end. He suddenly appeared with the three Hebrew men and walked around with them. So, what Nebuchadnezzar said looked like a god or a son of the gods in the fire - was likely Jesus in human form. (\"Daniel:3:23-28\"). Jesus often used the title \"Son of Man\" when referring to Himself. "profile name": "Damascus", "profile description": "", "profile bible infoscan": "The founder of the city of Damascus was Uz. Uz was the grandson of Shem and great-grandson of Noah (\"Genesis:9:18\" , \"Genesis:10:23\"). Damascus is first mentioned in the Bible in the story of Abraham. It was the oldest continually-inhabited city in the world and the capital of Syria (\"Isaiah:7:8\"). Damascus was situated in northern Palestine, northeast of the Sea of Galilee and Mount Hermon. It was an important city as three major caravan routes passed through the city, and it became a trade center with roads extending in different directions (\"Ezekiel:27:18\"). Two rivers, the Abana and Pharpar (\"2 Kings:5:12\"), provided Damascus with plenty of water for farming. Damascus is mentioned throughout the Old Testament, especially during the rules of King David and King Solomon and then during the rule of Assyria. All references to Damascus in the New Testament are associated with the Apostle Paul's conversion and ministry. Modern Damascus still has long streets with open-air markets that sell the same types of things sold in ancient times. However, there is now a strong influence of the Muslim culture, and their Great Mosque now stands on the site of a former Christian church.", "profile life lessons": "", "profile key scripture": "\"Saul's preaching became more and more powerful, and the Jews in Damascus couldn't refute his proofs that Jesus was indeed the Messiah.\""

His name means \"beautiful\" or \"pleasant,\" which speaks of Naaman after God miraculously healed him. He was a great warrior and highly respected because he had given victories to Aram. However, (\"2 Kings:5:1\") tells us something else about Naaman. \"The king of Aram had great admiration for Naaman, the commander of his army, because through him the Lord had given Aram great victories. But though Naaman was a mighty warrior, he suffered from leprosy.\" Yes, it would seem that Naaman had everything going for him except he there was one thing he could not defeat on his own; a serious skin disease called leprosy. Leprosy in that day was incurable. The leper was considered unclean and in some cases even quarantined. (Leviticus 13-14). Most likely because of his position, Naaman was allowed to stay in the city. At this time, Aramean raiders had invaded the land of Israel. One of the Israelites taken captive was a young girl who became a maid to Naaman's wife. One day the young girl told Naaman's wife that a prophet in Samaria could heal Naaman of his leprosy. Naaman shared what the young girl had said with the king. The king wrote a letter of introduction for Naaman to take to the king of Israel asking that Naaman be healed. This was a very humbling experience for Naaman. He was a proud warrior and Israel was the enemy! Even so, Naaman was desperate; he took expensive gifts and the letter to the King of Israel. The king of Israel felt threatened and believed the King of Syria was trying to pick a fight with him! In contrast, Elisha saw this as an opportunity to bring glory to God! (2 Kings 5:1-7). \"But when Elisha, the man of God, heard that the king of Israel had torn his clothes in dismay, he sent this message to him: \"Why are you so upset? Send Naaman to me, and he will learn that there is a true prophet here in Israel.\" (\"2 Kings:5:8\"). So Naaman went with his horses and chariots and waited at the door of Elisha's house. But Elisha sent a messenger out to him with this message: \"Go and wash yourself seven times in the Jordan River. Then your skin will be restored, and you will be healed of your leprosy.\" Naaman became angry and offended. Elisha would not even come to the door and talk with him; he sent a lowly servant instead! Naaman turned and went away in a rage! (\"2 Kings:5:10-12\"). Fortunately for Naaman, he was surrounded by wise officers who convinced him to follow Elisha's surprisingly simple instructions. \"But his officers tried to reason with him and said, \"Sir, if the prophet had told you to do something very difficult, wouldn't you have done it? So you should certainly obey him when he says simply, 'Go and wash and be cured!'\" So Naaman went down to the Jordan River and dipped himself seven times, as the man of God had instructed him. And his skin became as healthy as the skin of a young child, and he was healed!\" (\"2 Kings:5:13-14\"). Can you imagine what it would be like to see healthy skin instead of the leprosy? He was healed; not by the Syrian gods, but by the one true God of Israel! Naaman was so grateful that he returned to say thank you to Elisha and give him gifts. Naaman declared that there was no God in the entire world except in Israel. Elisha refused to take any gifts for a miracle that God alone had done! Then Naaman said, \"All right, but please allow me to load two of my mules with earth from this place, and I will take it back home with me. From now on I will never again offer burnt offerings or sacrifices to any other god except the Lord. However, may the Lord pardon me in this one thing: When my master the king goes into the temple of the god Rimmon to worship there and leans on my arm, may the Lord pardon me when I bow, too.\" \"Go in peace,\" Elisha said. So Naaman started home again. (2 Kings 17-19). The proud warrior Naaman had been humbled by God and chose to worship only him! In Luke 4:27, Jesus honored Naaman for humbling himself to obey God's instructions and receive his healing: \"And there were many lepers in Israel in the time of the prophet Elisha, but the only one healed was Naaman, a Syrian.\" (\"2 Kings:5:9\")", "profile life lessons": "Even the greatest and the most powerful men and women in the world can be humbled by God, just as Naaman was.", "profile key scripture": "Now I know that there is no God in all the world except in Israel. "profile name": "The Parable of the Sower", "profile description": "", "profile bible infoscan": "Agriculture was important in New Testament times. Jesus often referred to the land, using illustrations that were familiar to His audience. The Parable of the Sower was one of these illustrations. In Israel, plowing and sowing began in the middle of October at the time of the early rains and were then followed by harrowing (breaking up and smoothing the soil) and weeding. The later rains were vital for ripening the crops, and the rainy season usually ended in early April. Plowing was done by the workers with hoes or by a plow pulled by animals. Sowing took place after the first rains had softened the ground. If the farmer tried to plow before the rain, the plow-blade could not dig into the hard ground. There were two methods of sowing seed: by throwing the seeds by hand or using a seed-drill. When sowing by hand, the farmer walked along the furrows at a constant pace, pulling handfuls of seed from a bag at his side and throwing them over the soil. About 30 lbs of seed was used to a half acre of land. This is about half the quantity of seed normally used today. When using the seed drill method, at least three people were needed: one to direct the plow and push the handle down into the soil, one to direct the animals, and a third person to hold the seed bag on his shoulder and drop the seeds into the funnel which pointed down to the soil. The seeds would fall behind the plow-point where they were covered by the falling soil. Read \"Mark:4:14-20\" to learn the meaning of this parable.", "profile life lessons": "", "profile key scripture": "And the seed that fell on good soil represents those who hear and accept God's word and produce a harvest of thirty, sixty, or even a hundred times as much as had been planted!\""

"profile name": "Prodigal - Younger Son", "profile description": "The Prodigal Son asked for his inheritance from his father before his death. He then traveled to a distant land and wasted all of his money on wild living. He returned home, hoping his father would allow him to work as a servant. The father ran to his son and embraced him. ", "profile bible infoscan": "The Prodigal Son is the title of one of Jesus' many parables that He taught. (\"Luke:15:11\"). The prodigal, or lost son, disrespectfully asks for his inheritance even before his father's death. The title describes the young son's lifestyle; prodigal in this story means \"extremely wasteful.\" The son leaves home and carelessly spends his inheritance on sinful, wild living. After losing everything, he finds a job feeding pigs for a farmer. The Jews considered pigs to be unclean so this was the lowliest job that anyone could do. The son was so hungry that even the food he fed the pigs looked good to him. The young son had reached rock bottom. Jesus said that when the boy came to his senses, he returned home to his father and planned to ask him to be a hired servant - no longer feeling worthy to be called his son. While he was yet a long way off, the father saw him and was filled with love and compassion. He ran to his son and embraced and kissed him. Luke 15:22-24 says, \"But his father said to the servants, 'Quick! Bring the finest robe in the house and put it on him. Get a ring for his finger and sandals for his feet. And kill the calf we have been fattening. We must celebrate with a feast, for this son of mine was dead and has now returned to life. He was lost, but now he is found.' So the party began.\" Everyone seemed to be rejoicing except for the older son who was extremely angry with all that had happened. He believed that his younger brother did not deserve anything but punishment and rejection for his rebellion. \"His father said to him, 'Look, dear son, you have always stayed by me, and everything I have is yours. We had to celebrate this happy day. For your brother was dead and has come back to life! He was lost, but now he is found!'\" (\"Luke:15:31\"). The young son represents everyone who rebels against God, choosing to go their own way, and making unwise choices. The true focus of the story, however, should be on the forgiving, merciful, and patient nature of the father. He unconditionally loves his son and welcomes him home. Through this parable, Jesus defends God's offer of acceptance and salvation to everyone, regardless of who they are or what they have done. Many times, we are the Prodigal Son who need to experience the never ending forgiveness and mercy of our loving heavenly Father. Jonah was the only prophet in the Bible that we know of who ran away from God. (Jonah 1:1-3; Jonah 4:1-3).God did not call another prophet to deliver His message and let Jonah off the hook. "profile name": "Nineveh", "profile description": "Nineveh was a great city so large that it took three days to see it all! God saw all they did and changed His mind; Nineveh was saved!", "profile bible infoscan": "Nineveh was one of the oldest and greatest cities in the ancient world. The area was settled as early as 6000 BC and by 3000 BC had become an important religious center for worship of the Assyrian goddess Ishtar. Nineveh was described in the Book of Jonah as \"a great city\". (\"Jonah:1:2\"). It was the capital of the Assyrian Empire from 705 to 612 BC and located on the east bank of the Tigris River; modern day Iraq. Nineveh was established by Nimrod, a descendant of Noah, after the flood. (\"Genesis:10:9-12\"). The book of Jonah describes Nineveh as being so large that it took three days to see it all (\"Jonah:3:3\"). This description matches the size of the ruins of ancient Nineveh. It was a magnificent city lined with wide boulevards, large parks and gardens. Canals and aqueducts collected water from the hills about thirty miles away. There were eighteen canals designed to carry water to as many as 150,000 people who lived in Nineveh. Nineveh was also a walled and heavily gated city. It is estimated that the perimeter of Nineveh's wall was 7.5 miles long and 148 feet high in certain spots. There were fifteen gates that connected these city walls. Each of these gates was named after an Assyrian god. Jonah's message to the Ninevites was simple: \"Forty days from now Nineveh will be destroyed!\" (\"Jonah:3:4\"). The people of Nineveh believed Jonah's message. They called a fast and put on sackcloth, from the poor people to the rich and powerful. By the time word reached the king, much of the city had already repented. The king also believed Jonah's warning too. He removed his royal robes and put on mourning clothes. He then made a decree for all of Nineveh to fast and pray to God for mercy. Both men and animals were to be covered with sackcloth. All of the people were to cease from their wicked and violent ways. God saw all that they had done and changed His mind! He spared the city from judgment. It seems everyone except Jonah was happy. God told Jonah that He was showing pity for the people who did not know the difference between right and wrong (Jonah 3: 5-10; 4:11). In May of 612, the city was captured by the Medes and Babylonians during a three-month siege. Most of the people in the city were killed or made to be slaves. The Jewish prophet Nahum described the destruction and overthrow of Nineveh in \"Nahum:3:7\" .", "profile life lessons": "Love our enemies and pray that they will come to know him.", "profile key scripture": "\"Get up and go to the great city of Nineveh. "profile name": "Samaritans", "profile description": "The Samaritans are an ethno-religious group of the Holy Land, descended from ancient Semitic inhabitants of the region. The Samaritans follow Samaritanism, an Abrahamic religion, most closely related to Judaism.", "profile bible infoscan": "The Samaritans were people who lived in the Northern Kingdom of Israel. The Kingdom of Israel was split in two after the death of Solomon. Samaria eventually became the capital of the Northern Kingdom of Israel. Jerusalem was the capital of the Southern Kingdom of Judah. The Samaritans claim they descended from the Northern Israelite tribes of Ephraim and Manasseh. These were the two sons of Joseph. When the Assyrians conquered Samaria, they sent pagan people to occupy the land. The result was a mixture of faiths and beliefs. Some of the people followed the Law of Moses and worshiped Jehovah God. Others worshiped false gods and idols. Then there were also those who mixed both together! The Samaritans who did not worship idols also came up with their own version of worship. They only followed the first five books of the Old Testament called the Pentateuch. These books are Genesis, Exodus, Leviticus, Numbers, and Deuteronomy. They rejected the rest of the Old Testament books. They also made their own modifications to the Torah, which is the Law of Moses. Additionally, many of the Jews intermarried with the pagans. When the Temple was destroyed in Jerusalem by the Babylonians, Nehemiah refused to let the Samaritans help to rebuild it. The Samaritans then built their own Temple for worship on Mt.Gerizim. (\"2 Kings:17:5\") (\"Ezra:4:17\"). These are some of the main reasons that the Samaritan people were hated. They were considered to be impure, unclean, and half breeds by the Jews. During Jesus' time on earth, the hostility between the two groups was common. Jewish people would often bypass Samaria as they traveled between Galilee and Judea. This took them many miles out of their way! Jesus chose to travel directly through Samaria on His way to Galilee. There He talked with a Samaritan woman at a well. (\"John:4:4\"). In John 4:9, the Samaritan woman replied to Jesus's request for a drink of water. \"The woman was surprised, for Jews refuse to have anything to do with Samaritans. She said to Jesus, \"You are a Jew, and I am a Samaritan woman. Why are you asking me for a drink?\" She also told Jesus in John 4:19: \"Sir,\" the woman said, \"You must be a prophet. So tell me, why is it that you Jews insist that Jerusalem is the only place of worship, while we Samaritans claim it is here at Mount Gerizim, where our ancestors worshiped?\" The Samaritans believed that Mount Gerizim was the original Holy Place of the Israelites. All people would worship together in spirit and in truth, regardless of their differences. (\"John:4:21\"). Because of the woman's witness, the people in her town begged Jesus to stay and teach them. Jesus stayed for two days and many became believers! They declared Him to be the Savior of the world! (John 4:39-42). Jesus told His disciples to look around and see the fields ripe for harvesting. The fields represented the Samaritans and all people of the world. Anyone whose heart was open to hear the Gospel! (\"John:4:27\"). This was in contrast to a Jewish priest and a Levite Temple assistant who passed him by! Jesus then told the scribe to show that same kind of mercy to others. (Luke 10:25-37). In Luke 17:11-19, Jesus encountered ten lepers between Galilee and Samaria. He healed all of them, yet only one came back to thank Him. The Bible tells us that the man who returned was a Samaritan! "profile name": "The Tabernacle", "profile description": "The Tabernacle was the portable dwelling place for the divine presence of God and the Ark of the Covenant from the time of the Exodus from Egypt through the conquering of the land of Canaan. Built to specifications revealed by Yahweh to Moses at Mount Sinai, it accompanied the Israelites on their wanderings in the wilderness and their conquest of the Promised Land.", "profile bible infoscan": "The Tabernacle was the portable dwelling place for the divine presence of God and the Ark of the Covenant from the time of the Exodus from Egypt through the conquering of the land of Canaan. Built to specifications revealed by Yahweh to Moses at Mount Sinai, it accompanied the Israelites on their wanderings in the wilderness and their conquest of the Promised Land. There is no mention of the Tabernacle in the Bible after the destruction of Jerusalem and the Temple by the Babylonians in 587 BC. Within the Tabernacle was the Holy of Holies, housing the Ark of the Covenant, and an outer chamber called the Holy Place, with a golden lampstand, table for showbread, and the altar of incense. The English word \"tabernacle\" is derived from the Latin tabernaculum meaning \"tent\" or \"hut,\" which in ancient Roman religion was a ritual structure. The word sanctuary is also used for the Biblical tabernacle, as well as the phrase the \"tent of meeting.\" The commandments for construction of the Tabernacle are taken from the words in the Book of Exodus when God says to Moses: Have the people of Israel build me a holy sanctuary so I can live among them. You must build this Tabernacle and its furnishings exactly according to the pattern I will show you. (\"Exodus:25:8-9\") The more detailed description of a tabernacle is in (\"Exodus:25:1\") and (\"Exodus:35:1\"), which describes the Holy of Holies housing the Ark and the outer chamber, or Holy Place, with a seven-branched lampstand, table for showbread, and altar of incense. An enclosure containing the sacrificial altar surrounded these chambers. There was a set of strict rules to be followed for the Tabernacle set on the Old Testament. For example: \"For the LORD had said to Moses, 'Exempt the tribe of Levi from the census; do not include them when you count the rest of the Israelites. You must put the Levites in charge of the Tabernacle of the Covenant, along with its furnishings and equipment. They must carry the Tabernacle and its equipment as you travel, and they must care for it and camp around it. Whenever the Tabernacle is moved, the Levites will take it down and set it up again. Anyone else who goes too near the Tabernacle will be executed.'\" (Numbers 1:48-51) (\"Numbers:1:48-51\") Speaking of the Tabernacle, the great Jewish historian, Josephus wrote: \"...and great was the surprise of those who viewed these curtains at a distance, for they seemed not at all to differ from the color of the sky\" - Josephus (94 A.D.) Inside, the enclosure was divided into two areas, the Holy Place and the Most Holy Place, which were separated by a curtain. Inside the first area were the seven-branched oil lampstand on the left (south), a table for twelve loaves of show bread on the right (north) and the Altar of Incense (west), straight ahead before the dividing curtain. Beyond this curtain was the cube-shaped inner room known as the \"Holy of Holies,\" which housed the Ark of the Covenant. Inside the Ark were the two stone tablets brought down from Mount Sinai by Moses on which were written the Ten Commandments, a golden urn holding the manna, and Aaron's rod that budded and bore ripe almonds. (\"Hebrews:9:2-5\") The Tabernacle remained the dwelling place for God's presence until the Temple of Solomon was built in the 10th Century, B.C", "profile life lessons": "God calls us to a life of holiness.", "profile key scripture": "Samuel was sleeping in the Tabernacle near the Ark of God."
"profile name": "Sea of Galilee", "profile description": "", "profile bible infoscan": "In the Bible, the Sea of Galilee is referred to by four different names: the Sea of Chinnereth or Kinnereth (\"Numbers:34:11\" , \"Joshua:12:3\" , \"Joshua:13:27\"), the Lake of Gennesaret (\"Luke:5:1\"), the Sea of Tiberias (\"John:6:1\" , \"John:21:1\"), and the Sea of Galilee (\"Matthew:4:18\" , \"Mark:1:16\"). The Sea of Galilee is a fresh water lake that is fed by the Jordan River in the north. It is situated about 60 miles north of Jerusalem, and, because it is the deepest part of the northern Jordan Rift, the water collects there before flowing south into the Dead Sea. The surface of the Sea of Galilee is about 700 feet (230 meters) below the Mediterranean Sea -- and the floor of the lake is about 80 to 160 feet lower. The lake is about 13 miles long and eight miles wide at Magdala, the point where it is the widest. Except on the southern side, the lake is surrounded by steep cliffs and sharply rising mountains. On the east, the mountains rise to the Golan Heights and the fertile Hauran plateau, which reaches a height of 2,700 feet. This geographical formation often causes cool winds to rush down the slopes, causing sudden, violent storms on the warm surface of the lake. The high waves that result are like those that Jesus calmed (\"Mark:4:35-41\"). Jesus' earthly ministry was closely connected to the Sea of Galilee. The first disciples He called were part of the thriving fishing industry there: Simon Peter, Andrew, James, and John (\"Mark:1:16-20\"). On and around the Sea of Galilee, Jesus performed 18 of His 33 recorded miracles and spoke most of His teachings to His disciples and the crowds that followed Him. The Sea of Galilee is sometimes used as an illustration for how one should receive but also give and bless others in order to be \"living\" and not \"dead\" like the Dead Sea. Because the Sea of Galilee receives fresh water which then flows out into the Dead Sea, it is alive with fish and other creatures. The Dead Sea has no exit and is the lowest point on earth. It is also called the Salt Sea as a result of the high concentration of salt. It is not a favorable environment for animal life. In this regard, it is a \"Dead Sea.\"", "profile life lessons": "", "profile key scripture": "One day, as Jesus was walking along the shore of the Sea of Galilee, he saw Simon (Peter) and his brother Andrew throwing a net into the water (for they fished for a living). Jesus called out to them, \"Come, follow me, and I will show you how to fish for people!\""

Once cast or thrown, no one could argue with the results. Modern equivalents to casting lots would be throwing dice or flipping a coin. The practice of casting lots is mentioned seventy times in the Old Testament and seven times in the New Testament. Different objects were used to cast lots, depending on the location and customs, such as polished sticks, coins, cards, dice, etc. In the story of Jonah, the sailors cast lots to determine who was guilty of bringing a violent storm on the sea that threatened their very lives! \"Then the crew cast lots to see which of them had offended the gods and caused the terrible storm. When they did this, the lots identified Jonah as the culprit.\" An interesting fact is that in ancient Israel, the High Priest cast lots for important, uncertain decisions. It was part of the process of consulting God for the answer: This is the case when Zechariah the priest, father of John the Baptist, was chosen by lots to burn incense in the Temple. (\"Luke:1:8-9\"). Casting Lots is actually remembered by the Jewish people in the Feast of Purim. The word Purim means \"Lots\". The evil Haman cast lots in \"Esther:3:7\" to determine the best day to carry out his plan to destroy the Jewish people. The feast celebrates how Haman's evil plan was defeated by God and Queen Esther. In the New Testament, the soldiers cast lots for Jesus' clothes at His crucifixion. (\"John:19:23-24\"). The last time that casting lots is mentioned in the Bible was when the apostles asked God for direction in choosing between two people to replace Judas. (\"Acts:1:24-26\"). In our day, there isn't a need for casting lots. We are instructed to use the Bible, prayer and the indwelling Holy Spirit for guidance to make important choices and decisions. "profile name": "Tower of Babel", "profile description": "There was a time when people were building a tower to defy God and to show their greatness (\"Genesis:11:4\"). God recognizes the rebellion in the heart of the people and he confuses their languages. This caused the people to be scattered throughout the earth.", "profile bible infoscan": "The Tower of Babel was built in the plain of Shinar, which was an area in Mesopotamia. Stone and mortar were common building materials in Canaan; however, stone was in short supply in Mesopotamia. Archeological excavations indicate that mud brick and tar was used to build the tower. (\"Genesis:11:1-3\"). The tower was probably a ziggurat, which is a style of tower common in Mesopotamia. A ziggurat has a square base and slopes upwards. Ziggurat towers were often dedicated to a false god. In their minds, the design of the tower made it convenient for a god to \"come down\" to his temple, receive worship from the people, and then bless them. The tower served as a type of bridge between heaven and earth. The remains of over thirty ziggurat towers have been discovered throughout this region. The oldest one discovered is over 7,000 years old. It is not known for sure exactly when the Tower of Babel was built, but from the Bible we do know that it was several generations after Noah. Babel is a Hebrew word which means \"confusion\" or \"to confuse.\" Building a tower was not a sin; yet, the reason the tower was built was sinful. It was in direct disobedience to God's command for Noah's family to multiply and fill the earth after the flood. Instead, the people decided to stay in one place, build a great city and the tower, and then stay in one place. They also were filled with pride; wanting to be famous instead of bringing glory to God. (Genesis 11:4). The tower was not completed because God put a stop to it. He confused their language so they weren't able to communicate and understand each other any longer. (\"Genesis:11:5-9\").", "profile life lessons": "Remember that pride comes before a fall.", "profile key scripture": "\"Come, let's build a great city for ourselves with a tower that reaches into the sky.\""

The Bible says that Herod respected John and knew that he was good and holy. Herod often talked with John in prison. (\"Mark:6:20\"). Herod's wife Herodias hated John and devised a plot to have him killed. At Herod's birthday party, Herodias' daughter Salome danced for Herod and his guests. This pleased Herod so much that he promised to give Salome anything she wanted. Salome, by her mother's wicked influence, requested the head of John the Baptist. The king was trapped since he made the promise to Salome in front of his guests. He regrettably had John beheaded in prison. When John's disciples heard the news, they came to bury the body of John in a tomb.
