(\"Genesis:12:1-7\"). It was mentioned over 75 times in the Old Testament of the Bible. Ancient Canaan included the region between the Jordan River and the Mediterranean. This is roughly the present day Israel, the Palestinian territories, Lebanon, and coastal and southern Syria. The borders of the land were described in detail to Moses in \"Numbers:34:1-12\" . God reminded and reaffirmed His promises to Abraham many times through the years. \"I will confirm my covenant with you and your descendants after you, from generation to generation. This is the everlasting covenant: I will always be your God and the God of your descendants after you. And I will give the entire land of Canaan, where you now live as a foreigner, to you and your descendants. It will be their possession forever, and I will be their God.\" (\"Genesis:17:17\"). When Joshua's twelve spies scouted out the land, they found out the land was fertile with good soil for growing food. The spies described it as a bountiful land - a land flowing with milk and honey. (\"Numbers:13:25-27\"). \"When they came to the valley of Eshcol, they cut down a branch with a single cluster of grapes so large that it took two of them to carry it on a pole between them!\" (\"Numbers:13:23\"). They advised God's people to not try to possess the land, contrary to God's command and promise to give it to them. (Numbers 13:26-28, 31-33) This bad report caused the Israelite's to rebel. They wanted to return to Egypt instead of trusting God. This brought God's wrath and punishment upon them. God declared that none of them would enter Canaan. Instead, they would wander in the wilderness for 40 years! Only Joshua and Caleb were allowed to enter into Canaan. (\"Numbers:14:1-43\"). Canaan and the Canaanites are mentioned throughout the, mostly in the Pentateuch books (Genesis through Deuteronomy) and the books of Joshua and Judges. The part of the book of Genesis in the Hebrew Bible often called the Table of Nations describes the Canaanites as being descended from an ancestor called Canaan, the son of Ham, the grandson of Noah (\"Genesis:10:15-19\"). Israel's conquest of the Promised Land, Canaan, is described in the Old Testament books of Joshua, Judges, 1st and 2nd Samuel, and 1st and 2nd Kings. Your descendants will become many nations, and kings will be among them!\" (\"Genesis:17:4-6\"). God also changed Sarai's name to Sarah which means \"princess\". (\"Genesis:17:15-16\"). (\"Genesis:18:16-19\"). Oddly enough, in Genesis 20:1-18, we read that Abraham, a second time, was afraid and lied to King Abimelech just as he had the Egyptians. He told him to take Isaac and sacrifice him on Mount Moriah. Abraham obeyed God's instructions and demonstrated total trust in Him. Genesis 22:15-19 says, \"Then the angel of the Lord called again to Abraham from heaven. \"This is what the Lord says: Because you have obeyed me and have not withheld even your son, your only son, I swear by my own name that I will certainly bless you. I will multiply your descendants beyond number, like the stars in the sky and the sand on the seashore. Your descendants will conquer the cities of their enemies. And through your descendants all the nations of the earth will be blessed - all because you have obeyed me.\" Then they returned to the servants and traveled back to Beersheba, where Abraham continued to live.\" We read further of Abraham's amazing faith in Hebrews 11:17-19: \"It was by faith that Abraham offered Isaac as a sacrifice when God was testing him. Abraham, who had received God's promises, was ready to sacrifice his only son, Isaac, even though God had told him, \"Isaac is the son through whom your descendants will be counted.\" Abraham reasoned that if Isaac died, God was able to bring him back to life again. "profile name": "Persia", "profile description": "", "profile bible infoscan": "Cyrus the Great founded the First Persian Empire in the 6th century B.C. after overthrowing the Medes. The empire expanded to eventually rule over large portions of the ancient world, stretching from the Indus Valley in the east, to Thrace and Macedon on the northeastern border of Greece. At that time, it was the biggest empire in the world. In time, this empire would also control Egypt. A series of monarchs unified the tribes and groups by making a complex network of roads to move armies and commerce. From this empire, Cyrus the Great (Cyrus II of Persia) advanced to defeat the Median, the Lydian, and the Babylonian Empires. This opened the way for other conquests into Egypt and Asia Minor. The empire spanned the three continents: Asia, Africa, and Europe. The Persian Empire included the modern territories of Iran, Iraq, Syria, Jordan, Israel, Palestine, and Lebanon. These were all large centers of ancient Egypt. They would reach as far west as Libya, Turkey, Thrace, and Macedonia. It also reached much of the Black Sea coastal regions, Armenia, Georgia, Azerbaijan, much of Central Asia, Afghanistan, northern Saudi Arabia, and parts of western Pakistan. The Empire finally collapsed when Alexander the Great defeated the Persian armies at Granicus in 334 BC, followed by Issus (333 BC), and at Gaugamela (331 BC). Afterwards, he marched on Susa and Persepolis, which surrendered in early 330 BC. The nation of Persia would be modern day Iran. The Persia Empire (550-330 B.C.) was much larger beginning at the Indus River in the east and stretching as far west as the Aegean Sea in Asia Minor. The empire reached north to Southern Russia and south included Egypt to the Persian Gulf. There were four capital cities; Susa, Pasargadae, Ecbatana, and Persepolis. The story of Esther takes place in King Xerxes' fortress in Susa. \"Esther:1:1-2\" says, \"These events happened in the days of King Xerxes, who reigned over 127 provinces stretching from India to Ethiopia. He is responsible for developing Persia into a world empire. Cyrus authorized the Jews to return from exile to their homeland. This fulfilled the prophecy in Isaiah chapters 44-45. - Cambyses (530-522 B.C.) believed to be Artaxerxes of Ezra chapter 4. - Darius 1 (522- 486 B.C.) of Ezra chapter 6. - Xerxes (486-465 B.C.) is the king in the book of Esther. - Artaxerxes 1 (464- 423 B.C.) of Nehemiah chapters 1-2. "profile name": "The Book of Revelation", "profile description": "", "profile bible infoscan": "The Book of Revelation gives us a little look into the hidden things of God. Reading it is like peeking into the future (and the present) through a curtain that has been drawn back slightly. The type of literature or writing in Revelation is called Apocalyptic. This comes from the Greek word, \"Apocalypse,\" meaning \"unveiling\" or \"disclosure.\" Examples of Apocalyptic literature in the Old Testament include Daniel (chapters 7-12), Isaiah (chapters 24-27), Ezekiel (chapters 37-41), and Zechariah (chapters 9-12). The Book of Revelation uses symbols, images, and numbers to describe the end of the present age and the coming of God's future kingdom. One reason why the writer uses imagery is that the book was written in dangerous religious and political times, and it was safer to hide the message in images than to speak plainly. The images and the symbolism give the book a feeling of mystery, but the purpose of the book was not to confuse readers. It was written to inform and encourage readers in the face of opposition. The main theme of Revelation is that there are two warring powers: God and Satan. The overall message is that God is all-powerful. God's majesty and power are shown in the images of the throne and the angelic choruses who bow before the throne and call Him God Almighty. Jesus Christ, the rider on the white horse, is the central figure in the army of God the King. Nothing the devil (Satan) can do (no matter how strong) can stop the purposes of God from being fulfilled. In the final battle, Satan and his followers are completely destroyed by fire from heaven (\"Revelation:20:7-10\"). The Book of Revelation contains seven visions: 1. Christ encourages the earthly Church to remain loyal (\"Revelation:1-3\"). 2. Christ the Lamb opens seven seals on a scroll which hold the destinies of individuals and nations, including disasters (\"Revelation:4-7\"). 3. Seven angels blow trumpets, and more disasters occur (\"Revelation:8-11\"). 4. The vision that symbolizes the persecution of the Church (\"Revelation:12-14\"). 5. The vision in which seven bowls pour out God's wrath (\"Revelation:15-16\"). 6. The vision about the judgment of Babylon (which symbolizes the world in rebellion) (\"Revelation:17:1\" through \"Revelation:19:10\"). 7. The final vision about the final victory, final judgment, and final blessing (\"Revelation:19:11\" through \"Revelation:22\" author of the Book of Revelation is believed to be John, the apostle who was exiled to the island of Patmos (\"Revelation:1:9\"). This includes the Passover sacrifice, sin offering, guilt offering, release of the scapegoat, burnt offering, peace offering, red heifer, heave offering, meal offering, dough offering, drink offering, incense offering, thank offering, and more throughout the religious calendar. It was one of the priest's duties to keep the incense burning on the altar in front of the Most Holy Place in the Temple. The priests supplied the altar with fresh incense before the morning sacrifice and again after the evening sacrifice. As with Zechariah, the assignment to burn incense was determined by casting lots. This meant a priest might never have been chosen to perform this task honored assignment in his lifetime. For Zechariah to have been chosen to enter the holy place and burn the incense at the time Gabriel was to announce the birth of their son was surely an act of God. (Luke 18-11). Some other duties of the priests included blessing God's people, collecting tithes, and reading God's Law to the people. (Numbers 6:22-26; Deuteronomy 31: 9-12; Hebrews 7:5; Nehemiah 8:2-3). When a priest sinned, he brought guilt upon himself and upon the entire community. (\"Leviticus:4:3\"). They served as Temple assistants to the priests and did different jobs to assist them. The Levites took care of the temple and served as musicians, singers, gatekeepers, and helped prepare the sacrifices. They also read the Book of the Law to the people and explained the meaning to them (\"Nehemiah:8:7-8\"). The role of the priest is no longer necessary today because of Jesus. He is God's perfect sacrifice that took away the sin of the world. When Jesus died, the Temple veil or curtain was torn in two giving all believers in Christ access into the Holy of Holies, the very presence of God! \"So then, since we have a great High Priest who has entered heaven, Jesus the Son of God, let us hold firmly to what we believe. Besides being Jewish, he was also a Roman citizen, and after he became a Christian, he was referred to by his Roman name, Paul (\"Acts:13:9\"). Paul became a great preacher of the Gospel and teacher of Christianity. He made three main missionary journeys (Acts 13-21), preaching, establishing, and then visiting churches in different parts of the Roman Empire. He stayed in prison for over two years before he appeared before the new governor named Festus and then he even testified before King Agrippa! Both men decided that Paul had done nothing worthy of death and would have let him go, except Paul had appealed to Caesar to hear his case. So, Paul was now off to Rome! (Acts 24-26). Paul and other prisoners were placed under custody of a Roman officer named Julius as they traveled by ship to Rome. Julius was kind to Paul and allowed him to go ashore when they docked in Sidon to visit friends who cared for Paul's needs. Along the way, a terrible storm battered their ship for several days. Paul had told the ship's captain and the officers to turn back but they would not listen. An angel appeared to Paul one night. On the island, Paul survived a poisonous snake bite and by God's power, healed all who were sick on the island. This included the father of the chief official of the island, Publius. Three months later, they sailed again on a new ship toward Rome. (Acts 28:1-8). When Paul arrived in Rome, he was allowed to stay in his own home and was guarded by a soldier. For the next two years, Paul received people into his home and boldly testified about the Kingdom of God and no one tried to stop him! This man whom God changed much did much to change the world for God. (\"Acts:28:9-31\"). When Paul arrived in Rome, he was under house arrest and chained to a Roman guard. Mamertine was a filthy and vile dungeon which was where criminals were held for a short time before they were executed. "profile name": "Babylon/Ishtar Gate", "profile description": "", "profile bible infoscan": "The name Babylon is the Greek form of the Hebrew word \"babel,\" which means \"confused.\" Geography: Babylon, the capital of the ancient land Babylonia in Mesopotamia, was once a great city situated on the Euphrates River. It was about fifty miles south of modern Baghdad. Archeologists discovered the ruins of this huge city in the 19th century. Babylonia was a long, narrow country that covered an area of about 8,000 square miles. At its widest point, it was about 40 miles! It was bordered by Assyria (north), Elam (east), the Arabian Desert (south and west), and the Persian Gulf (southeast). History: Abraham lived in Ur, an ancient city in Babylon, and moved to Haran. From there he moved to the land of Canaan. He obeyed God's command and believed God's promise that he would become the father of a great nation (\"Genesis:12:0\" From about 1270 BC, Assyria became the leading power in the ancient world. However, Babylonia became independent again around 626 BC under the leadership of Nabopolassar. The Babylonian empire became the dominant power in the Near East and entered into her \"golden age.\" In 605 BC, Nebuchadnezzar ll, the son of Nabolpolassar, became king and ruled for 44 years. He conquered other nations, took their treasures, and built Babylon into one of the greatest cities of the world. The famous hanging gardens of Babylon were known to the Greeks as one of the seven wonders of the world. In 587 BC, the Babylonians destroyed Jerusalem and took the leading citizens captive to Babylon. Daniel was one of these captives. During this 70-year captivity, the Persians conquered Babylonia and became the leading power instead. Religion: Throughout their history, the Babylonians achieved a high level of civilization. Their religion centered around temples where they worshiped various gods and goddesses, including Ishtar, the goddess of love and war. The Ishtar Gate, one of the eight entrances to the inner city of Babylon, was built during the reign of Nebuchadnezzar ll (605-562 BC). It was dedicated to the Babylonian goddess Ishtar. It was actually a double gate, constructed of blue glazed tiles with rows of dragons and aurochs (a type of large, wild cattle). The doors and roofs of the gate were made of cedar wood. The walls, which lined the Processional Way that ran through the gate, were covered in lions on glazed bricks. Originally the gate, as part of the Walls of Babylon, was considered one of the Seven Wonders of the World. However, in the 6th century AD, the Lighthouse of Alexandria took the title.", "profile life lessons": "", "profile key scripture": "\"Then the watchman said, 'Babylon is fallen! The rocky island of Malta is located in the Mediterranean Sea is about sixty-two miles south of Sicily and 1200 miles from Jerusalem. The island is only about 17 miles long and 9 miles wide. Throughout history, Malta's location and good harbors in the middle of the Mediterranean have given it great strategic importance. Malta gained independence from the United Kingdom in 1964 and became a republic in 1974. Malta was admitted to the United Nations in 1964 and to the European Union in 2004. In 2008, it became part of the Eurozone, which is a group of European nations whose national currency is the euro. "profile name": "Noah", "profile description": "The world was fraught with evil. So evil, in fact, that God vows to destroy the world, saving only Noah. Noah obeys, displaying his unwavering faith in God.", "profile bible infoscan": "Noah was the son of Lamech, who was a descendant of Adam's son Seth. Noah's name actually means \"relief.\" Noah's grandfather was Methuselah who lived for 969 years. Noah was married and had three sons named Shem, Ham, and Japheth when he was 500 years old! (\"Genesis:5:25-32\"). During the time of Noah, God looked at what was going on in the world He created and finally said enough is enough! \"The Lord observed the extent of human wickedness on the earth, and He saw that everything they thought or imagined was consistently and totally evil. So the Lord was sorry He had ever made them and put them on the earth. It broke his heart.\" (\"Genesis:6:5-6\"). He decided to wipe all living things off the earth - except for Noah, who was a righteous light in the sinful darkness. Noah found favor with God. The Bible tells us that Noah was righteous, the only blameless person living on earth. He walked in close fellowship with God. (\"Genesis:6:8-13\"). In the book of Ezekiel, Noah's righteousness is twice mentioned along with Daniel and Job. (\"Ezekiel:14:14\"). God spoke to Noah and gave him specific instructions to build an ark or large boat. \"Build a large boat from cypress wood and waterproof it with tar, inside and out. Then construct decks and stalls throughout its interior. Make the boat 450 feet long, 75 feet wide, and 45 feet high. Leave an 18-inch opening below the roof all the way around the boat. Put the door on the side, and build three decks inside the boat - lower, middle, and upper.\" (\"Genesis:6:14-16\"). God told Noah that He was about to cover the earth with a flood that would destroy every living, breathing thing. He said that Noah and his family would enter the ark, along with a male and female of every kind of animal. Noah was charged with keeping them alive while on the ark during the flood. He had to gather enough food for his family and the animals. In addition, he was to bring approved types of animals to eat and to sacrifice to God as an offering. Noah didn't cut any corners or take any shortcuts; he did everything exactly as God commanded him. (\"Genesis:6:22\"). Noah had to trust God completely. It is unlikely that people of that day had even seen rain, let alone a flood! Hebrews 11:7 tells us: \"It was by faith that Noah built a large boat to save his family from the flood. He obeyed God, who warned him about things that had never happened before. By his faith Noah condemned the rest of the world, and he received the righteousness that comes by faith.\" It would seem that Noah was both a preacher in word and by action warning the world of the coming judgment as they watched the ark take shape. Surely, people stopped to ask Noah what he was doing and he took advantage of the opening to talk about God and His plan. No doubt many people mocked Noah as he labored to complete the huge task he was given. \"2 Peter:2:5\" says, \"And God did not spare the ancient world - except for Noah and the seven others in his family. Noah warned the world of God's righteous judgment. So God protected Noah when he destroyed the world of ungodly people with a vast flood\" When the ark was finished, God instructed Noah to take his family and all of the animals into the ark. The door was not closed. We can see God's love and mercy here as he waited to see if any other people would heed Noah's warning and enter the ark to be saved. After seven days, it began to rain and God shut the door behind them. The rain would not stop for forty days and nights. Noah was 600 years old when the flood covered the earth. (\"Genesis:7:1-16\"). The waters rose and increased greatly on the earth, and the ark floated safely on the surface. The water kept rising until the water was 22 feet about the highest mountain peaks! Every living thing that moved on land perished - birds, livestock, wild animals, all the creatures that swarm over the earth, and all humanity. God wiped out everyone and everything outside the ark of safety. Only Noah and those with him in the ark survived. The waters flooded the earth for 150 days. (\"Genesis:7:17-24\"). But God did not forget Noah, his family, and all the animals in the ark. When the forty days were over, He sent a wind over the earth. The torrential rains from the sky and the underground waters stopped flowing; the floodwaters then started to recede. \"After 150 days, exactly five months from the time the flood began, the boat came to rest on the mountains of Ararat. Two and a half months later, as the waters continued to go down, other mountain peaks became visible. (\"Genesis:8:3-5\"). Forty days later, Noah opened the window and released a raven. The bird flew back and forth until the floodwaters on the earth had dried up.Then Noah released a dove, but the dove could find no place to land because the water still covered the ground and it returned to Noah. Seven days later, Noah released the dove and it returned to him in the evening with a fresh olive leaf in its beak. Noah knew that the floodwaters were almost gone. He waited another seven days and then released the dove again. This time it did not come back. (\"Genesis:8:6-12\"). When Noah was 601 years old, ten and a half months after the flood began, the floodwaters had almost dried up from the earth. Two more months went by, and at last the earth was dry! God told Noah and his family to leave the boat and to release all of the animals so they could multiply and fill the earth! (\"Genesis:8:13-17\"). \"Then Noah built an altar to the LORD and, taking some of all the clean animals and clean birds, he sacrificed burnt offerings on it. The LORD smelled the pleasing aroma and said in his heart: 'I will never again curse the ground because of the human race, even though everything they think or imagine is bent toward evil from childhood. I will never again destroy all living things'\" (\"Genesis:8:20-21\"). God blessed Noah and his sons and told them to multiply and repopulate the earth! (\"Genesis:9:1\"). He made a covenant with Noah, his sons, and all the animals on the boat. \"Yes, I am confirming my covenant with you. Never again will floodwaters kill all living creatures; never again will a flood destroy the earth.\" (\"Genesis:9:11\"). God then said that a rainbow in the clouds would be a sign of this covenant. \"When I send clouds over the earth, the rainbow will appear in the clouds, and I will remember my covenant with you and with all living creatures. Never again will the floodwaters destroy all life. When I see the rainbow in the clouds, I will remember the eternal covenant between God and every living creature on earth.\" (\"Genesis:9:12-17\") Even though Noah was seen as righteous in God's eyes, he was still human, and it wasn't long before Noah sinned before God and became drunk. Ham then sinned against his father and Noah pronounced a curse against Ham's son, Canaan. (\"Genesis:9:18-27\"). The Bible tells us Noah lived 350 years after the flood, making him 950 years old. "profile name": "Boaz", "profile description": "Boaz was related to Naomi and he ended up marrying Ruth.", "profile bible infoscan": "Boaz was a hero that came to the rescue of Naomi and Ruth! Boaz showed kindness to Ruth when he discovered her gathering grain in his fields. He ordered his workers to not bother her. Then he told them to purposely drop barley from their bundles for her to gather. Boaz spoke a blessing to Ruth for being loyal and kind to Naomi. (Ruth 1-4). By Jewish custom, Boaz as a close relative should redeem, or buy back, the property of Naomi. This is known as a kinsman-redeemer. He would also be responsible to marry Ruth and care for her. And, when possible, raise up an heir to carry on the family name of the person that died. This was a commitment that not all men were willing to undertake. (\"Leviticus:25:25\"). In the case of Ruth and Boaz, there was a kinsman-redeemer more closely related to Naomi. He had the first right to buy her land and marry Ruth. Boaz went to the city gate, where legal matters were conducted in ancient Israel. Boaz asked the other relative if he intended to purchase Naomi's land and marry Ruth. The relative said he could not. This allowed Boaz, who was next in line, to redeem the land and marry Ruth. Boaz married Ruth and God blessed them with a son named Obed. This son carried on the family name of Naomi's husband that had died. As a redeemer, Boaz is considered to be a symbol of Jesus, our Redeemer. Ruth and Boaz's son, Obed, was the father of Jesse, and grandfather of David. Boaz is mentioned in both the Gospel of Matthew and the Gospel of Luke as an ancestor of Jesus. 'Go in peace and may God bless your request.' God remembered Hannah and gave her a son, and she named him Samuel. Hannah kept her promise and gave Samuel back to God. When Samuel was older she went back to the place where she had prayed and said to Eli the priest, 'Do you remember me? I am the woman that cried and prayed for this child and He answered my prayer. "profile name": "Pilate", "profile description": "Pontius Pilate was a Roman governor of Judea. When Jesus was brought before him to be judged, Pilate was convinced that Jesus hadn't done anything to deserve the death sentence. However, he didn't want to make the Jews angry and damage his career, so he handed Jesus over to be executed (Matthew 27:26).", "profile bible infoscan": "Pontius Pilate was the 5th Roman governor of Judea from A.D. 26-36. He governed the area of Judea in which Jerusalem was situated. As governor, he had absolute authority over the non-Roman citizens in his district. Pilate was not popular with the Jews as he carried out his policies stubbornly -- but when the Jews opposed him, he often backed down, showing his weakness of character. We know Pilate was married because his wife warned him to have nothing to do with \"that innocent man\" (Jesus) as she had suffered a terrible nightmare about Him (\"Matthew:27:19\"). Jews could not be executed without the approval from the Roman authorities (\"John:18:31\"), and that is why the Jewish leaders brought Jesus to Pilate to pronounce the death sentence (\"Mark:14:64\"). Pilate was convinced that Jesus had not done anything that deserved the death sentence, and Pilate tried to release Him. However, he didn't want to make the Jews angry in case it damaged his reputation and his career. When the Jews insisted on Jesus' crucifixion, Pilate handed Him over to be executed (\"Matthew:27:26\"). Pilate showed weakness of character in that, although he had the power to set Jesus free, he pleased the crowd and acted selfishly. He \"washed his hands\" of the matter and did not accept responsibility for his actions (\"Matthew:27:24\"). He went against what he knew was right and chose to do wrong.", "profile life lessons": "Have the strength to stand up for what you believe to be right.", "profile key scripture": "Pilate saw that he wasn't getting anywhere, and that a riot was developing. So he sent for a bowl of water and washed his hands before the crowd, saying, 'I am innocent of this man's blood. The responsibility is yours!'"
"profile name": "Gold, Frankincense, and Myrrh", "profile description": "", "profile bible infoscan": "You've heard the Christmas songs, so you know what three gifts the Magi brought Jesus. But do you know why these three items WERE those gifts? It is that these three gifts were suitable for a king. GOLD: a precious and expensive gift fit for a king. Gold is mentioned over 500 times in the Bible, more than any other metal. It was used to make very important objects: the high priest's vest (\"Exodus:28:5\"), crowns (\"Psalms:21:3\"), chains (\"Genesis:41:42\"), and coins (\"1 Chronicles:21:25\"). It was also used in the building and furnishing of Solomon's Palace and the Temple. FRANKINCENSE: a gift often used in religious rites. Frankincense is taken from the Boswellia tree. The frankincense is obtained by cutting into the bark and collecting the resin from the tree. When this substance hardens, it is gathered and used as incense. Frankincense was part of the sacred anointing oil (\"Exodus:30:34\"). It was used in sacrificial offerings (\"Leviticus:2:1\") as a fumigant during animal sacrifices (\"Exodus:30:7\") and also as a perfume (\"Song of Songs:3:6\"). MYRRH: was a spice used to anoint a body for burial. Myrrh is an extract from the resin of Commiphora trees, a stiff-branched tree with white flowers and fruit like plums. After it is extracted from the wood, it hardens and can be used as an article for trade. Myrrh was used in embalming (\"John:10:39\"), as an ingredient in anointing oil (\"Exodus:30:23\"), and as perfume (\"Psalms:45:8\" , \"Proverbs:7:17\"). According to \"Mark:15:23\" , the drink offered to Jesus before His crucifixion was \"wine mingled with myrrh.\"", "profile life lessons": "", "profile key scripture": "They entered the house and saw the child with his mother, Mary, and they bowed down and worshiped him. Then they opened their treasure chests and gave him gifts of gold, frankincense, and myrrh."

Through Paul, God healed Publius' father, showing His power and love to Publius and the people of Malta.", "profile bible infoscan": "Publius was the chief official of the island of Malta. He welcomed and treated Paul and the ship's crew and passengers with kindness. Paul was invited to spend three days at Publius' estate. The father of Publius was ill; Paul laid hands on him, prayed and he was healed! Paul then prayed for all the sick on the island and they were healed too. Publius and the people of Malta honored Paul and gave the passengers and crew all the supplies they needed to continue their trip to Rome. (\"Acts:28:1-10\").", "profile life lessons": "If you have faith, like Paul did, God will do great things through you -- even miracles, if you will believe.", "profile key scripture": "As it happened, Publius's father was ill with fever and dysentery. "profile name": "Burning Bush", "profile description": "", "profile bible infoscan": "The burning bush was an extraordinary manifestation of God's divine presence and glory. Moses was surprised to see the flames, but he was even more surprised that the bush did not burn. This can be seen as a symbol of God's people--burned but not consumed, cast down but not destroyed (\"2 Corinthians:4:9\"). Through the fire, God gave Moses a gracious call to which Moses returned a ready answer (\"Exodus:3:4\"). In his approach to God, he was deeply affected and aware of the distance between him and God (\"Exodus:3:5\"). At first, Moses saw a dazzling burning bush and was not afraid. But once he knew God was in it, he became afraid, hid his face, and showed reverence to God. The closer one gets to God, the more one has cause for worship. In His gracious call to Moses, God instructed him to go back to Egypt and lead His people out of bondage.", "profile life lessons": "", "profile key scripture": "\"Do not come any closer,\" the Lord warned. \"Take off your sandals, for you are standing on holy ground.\""
"profile name": "Golgotha", "profile description": "", "profile bible infoscan": "Golgotha is the place where Jesus was crucified, a hill just outside the walls of Jerusalem (\"Mark:15:22\"). Golgotha means \"place of the skull.\" The place is also referred to as \"Calvary,\" which is English for the Latin word \"calvaria,\" meaning \"skull.\" No one really knows why Golgotha (Calvary) was called the \"place of the skull.\" It has been suggested that it was a place of execution or that it was near a cemetery or that the outcropping of rock looks like the shape of a human skull.", "profile life lessons": "", "profile key scripture": "Carrying the cross by himself, he went to the place called Place of the Skull (in Hebrew, Golgotha)."
